<tbody><tr>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:left;"><b><a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker</a> before election</b><br />
<p><a href="/wiki/Newt_Gingrich" title="Newt Gingrich">Newt Gingrich</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(US)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party (US)">Republican</a>
</p>
</td>
<td style="width:50%; text-align:right;"><b>Elected <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">Speaker</a></b> <br />
<p><a href="/wiki/Dennis_Hastert" title="Dennis Hastert">Dennis Hastert</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(US)" class="mw-redirect" title="Republican Party (US)">Republican</a>
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>1998 United States House of Representatives elections</b> were part of the <a href="/wiki/Midterm_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="Midterm elections">midterm elections</a> held during <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>'s second term. They were a major disappointment to the Republicans, who were expecting to gain seats due to the embarrassment Clinton suffered during the <a href="/wiki/Monica_Lewinsky_scandal" class="mw-redirect" title="Monica Lewinsky scandal">Monica Lewinsky scandal</a>, and the "<a href="/wiki/Six-year_itch" title="Six-year itch">six-year itch</a>" effect observed in most second-term midterm elections. However, the Republicans lost five seats to the Democrats, but retained a narrow majority in the House. A wave of Republican discontent with Speaker <a href="/wiki/Newt_Gingrich" title="Newt Gingrich">Newt Gingrich</a> prompted him to resign shortly after the election; he was replaced by Congressman <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Hastert" title="Dennis Hastert">Dennis Hastert</a> of Illinois.
</p><p>The campaign was marked by Republican attacks on the morality of President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>, with Independent Counsel <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Starr" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenneth Starr">Kenneth Starr</a> having released his report on the Lewinsky scandal and House leaders having initiated an inquiry into whether <a href="/wiki/Impeachment" title="Impeachment">impeachable</a> offenses had occurred. However, exit polls indicated that most voters opposed impeaching Clinton, and predictions of high Republican or low Democratic turnout due to the scandal failed to materialize.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Some speculate that the losses reflected a backlash against the Republicans for attacking the popular President Clinton. With the Republicans having lost 4 House seats and failing to gain any seats in the Senate, it was the first time since <a href="/wiki/1934_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections" title="1934 United States House of Representatives elections">1934</a> that the non-presidential party failed to gain congressional seats in a mid-term election. It was also the first time since <a href="/wiki/1822_United_States_House_of_Representatives_elections" class="mw-redirect" title="1822 United States House of Representatives elections">1822</a> that the non-presidential party had failed to gain seats in the mid-term election of a President's second term.
</p><p>Seats picked up by the Democrats included <span data-sort-value="Kansas03&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Kansas%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Kansas&#39;s 3rd congressional district">Kansas's&#160;3rd district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Nevada01&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Nevada%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Nevada&#39;s 1st congressional district">Nevada's&#160;1st district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Pennsylvania13&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_13th_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania&#39;s 13th congressional district">Pennsylvania's&#160;13th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="New Mexico03&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/New_Mexico%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="New Mexico&#39;s 3rd congressional district">New Mexico's&#160;3rd district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="New Jersey12&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/New_Jersey%27s_12th_congressional_district" title="New Jersey&#39;s 12th congressional district">New Jersey's&#160;12th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Kentucky04&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Kentucky&#39;s 4th congressional district">Kentucky's&#160;4th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Mississippi04&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Mississippi%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Mississippi&#39;s 4th congressional district">Mississippi's&#160;4th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="California01&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/California%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 1st congressional district">California's&#160;1st district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Wisconsin02&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Wisconsin%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Wisconsin&#39;s 2nd congressional district">Wisconsin's&#160;2nd district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Washington01&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Washington%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Washington&#39;s 1st congressional district">Washington's&#160;1st district</a></span>, and <span data-sort-value="Washington03&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Washington%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Washington&#39;s 3rd congressional district">Washington's&#160;3rd district</a></span>. The Republicans, however, picked up seats in <span data-sort-value="Kentucky06&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Kentucky%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Kentucky&#39;s 6th congressional district">Kentucky's&#160;6th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Wisconsin08&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Wisconsin%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Wisconsin&#39;s 8th congressional district">Wisconsin's&#160;8th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="California03&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/California%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 3rd congressional district">California's&#160;3rd district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="California36&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/California%27s_36th_congressional_district" title="California&#39;s 36th congressional district">California's&#160;36th district</a></span>, <span data-sort-value="Pennsylvania15&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania%27s_15th_congressional_district" title="Pennsylvania&#39;s 15th congressional district">Pennsylvania's&#160;15th district</a></span>, and <span data-sort-value="North Carolina08&#160;!"><a href="/wiki/North_Carolina%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="North Carolina&#39;s 8th congressional district">North Carolina's&#160;8th district</a></span>.
</p>
